                  </form> is a noun of place, [and of time,] as well as an inf. n.: [i. e.] it signifies [<hi rend="ital">A place,</hi> and <hi rend="ital">a time, of drinking:</hi> or] the <hi rend="ital">quarter</hi> (<foreign lang="ar">وَجْه</foreign>) <hi rend="ital">whence one drinks:</hi> (S, TA:) and <hi rend="ital">a place to which one comes to drink at a river</hi> or <hi rend="ital">rivulet:</hi> (TA:) and

                  <hi rend="ital">A day of vehement heat, in which is drunk more water than at other times.</hi> (TA.)    </entryFree>27:T2fb1,<entryFree id="n22024" key="شَرِبَ" type="main">     
                  <form>       
                     <itype>1</itype>        
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">شَرِبَ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form>, (S, A, K, &amp;c.,) aor.      
    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Ba" lang="ar">شَرَبَ</orth>
                  </form>, (A, K,) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">شُرْبٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">شَرْبٌ</foreign> (S, A, Msb, K, &amp;c.) and <foreign lang="ar">شِرْبٌ</foreign>, (S, A, K,) agreeably with three different readings of the Kur lvi. 55, (S, TA,) the first of which (with damm) is that generally obtaining, (Fr, TA,) and is the only one admitted by Jaafar Ibn-Mohammad, notwithstanding which the second form (with fet-h) is said by MF to be the most chaste as well as the most agreeable with analogy, (TA,) or the second (with fet-h) is an inf. n., and the first is a simple subst., (AO, S, Msb, K,) and so is the third, (AO, S, K,) and <foreign lang="ar">مَشْرَبٌ</foreign>, (S, K,) which is <pb n="1526"/> also a n. of place [and of time], (S,) and <foreign lang="ar">تَشْرَابٌ</foreign>, (S K, TA,) a form used when muchness of the act is meant, (TA,) and <foreign lang="ar">تِشْرَابٌ</foreign>, which is anomalous, (TA voce <foreign lang="ar">بَيَّنَ</foreign>, q. v.,) <hi rend="ital">He drank,</hi> (KL, PS, TK,) or <hi rend="ital">he swallowed,</hi> syn. <foreign lang="ar">جَرِعَ</foreign>, (A, K, [but the former meaning is evidently intended by this explanation, and such I shall assume to be the case in giving the explanations of the derivatives in the A and K. &amp;c.,]) water, &amp;c., (S,) or a liquid, properly <hi rend="ital">by sucking in,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">sipping;</hi> and <hi rend="ital">otherwise</hi> tropically; (Msb;) [generally, <hi rend="ital">gulping</hi> it; for] you say, <foreign lang="ar">شَرِبَ المَآءَ فِى كَرَّةٍ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">He drank the water at once,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">at a single draught</hi>]; and <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n22024-1" target="تشرّبهُ" n="1" type="8" subtype="FSOTF" lang="ar" select="n22024"/>فِى مُهْلَةٍ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">He drank it leisurely,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">gently,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">slowly</hi>]: (Mgh:) <foreign lang="ar">شُرْبٌ</foreign> signifies the <hi rend="ital">conveying to one's inside, by means of his mouth, that in the case of which chewing is not practicable:</hi> (KT:) [but] Es-Sarakustee says, one does not say of a bird <foreign lang="ar">شَرِبَ المَآءَ</foreign>, but <foreign lang="ar">حَسَاهُ</foreign>. (Msb.) In the saying of Aboo-Dhu-eyb, describing clouds, <quote>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">شَرِبْنَ بِمَآءِ البَحْرِ ثُمَّ تَرَفَّعَتْ</foreign>
                     </L> 
                  </quote> [which is evidently best rendered <hi rend="ital">They drank of the water of the sea, then rose aloft,</hi> agreeably with what has been stated respecting <foreign lang="ar">بِ</foreign> in the sense of <foreign lang="ar">مِنْ</foreign> in p. 143, it is said that] the <foreign lang="ar">ب</foreign> is redundant, or, as <foreign lang="ar">رَوِينَ</foreign> is rendered trans. by means of <foreign lang="ar">بِ</foreign>, [though I do not think that this is the case unless <foreign lang="ar">بِ</foreign> be used as meaning “ by means of, ” and I do not remember to have met with an instance of it,] <foreign lang="ar">شَرِبْنَ</foreign> is thus rendered trans. (TA.) [See a similar ex. in the 28th verse of the Mo'allakah of 'Antarah, EM p. 232.
